Second, we identified repeat contigs with paired ends that uniquely connected two other scaffolded contigs. If the length of the repeat contig and the estimated size of the gap were similar, the gap was filled by this repeat. Any remaining repeat contigs that were not used for gap filling were added into the final set of scaffolds.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec20">Chromosome anchoring along the cucumber genetic map.</h3><p>The marker sequences in the cucumber genetic map were aligned against the scaffold sequences using BLASTN at an <i>E</i>-value cutoff of 1 Ã 10<sup>â20</sup>. Hits with coverage &gt;30% and identity &gt;90% were considered mapped markers. Based on the mapped markers, the scaffold sequences were anchored on the cucumber chromosomes. During this process, the scaffolds with mapped markers that showed inconsistent genetic positions were manually checked by paired-end relationships; the incorrect scaffold was then split.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec21">FISH analysis.</h3><p>The FISH protocol was described in a previous study<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 16" title="Ren, Y. et al. An integrated genetic and cytogenetic map of the cucumber genome. PLoS One 4, e5795 (2009)." href="/articles/ng.475#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d17306e3247">16</a></sup>. To better visualize the segmental inversion, we chose chromosome spreads where chromosome 5 appeared in a straight form. Instead of showing all chromosomes<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 16" title="Ren, Y. et al. An integrated genetic and cytogenetic map of the cucumber genome. PLoS One 4, e5795 (2009)." href="/articles/ng.475#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d17306e3251">16</a></sup>, only chromosome 5 is shown in <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/ng.475#Fig1">Figure 1b</a> of this study. In addition, the image was taken in a higher resolution. Scale bars represent 1 Î¼m, as compared to 3 Î¼m previously<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 16" title="Ren, Y. et al. An integrated genetic and cytogenetic map of the cucumber genome. PLoS One 4, e5795 (2009)." href="/articles/ng.475#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d17306e3258">16</a></sup>. Red and green signals were detected with anti-digoxigenin antibody coupled to rhodamine (Roche) and by anti-avidin antibody conjugated with FITC (Vector Laboratories), respectively.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec22">Identification of repetitive elements in the cucumber genome.</h3><p>Four <i>de novo</i> software packages, ReAS<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Li, R. et al. ReAS: Recovery of ancestral sequences for transposable elements from the unassembled reads of a whole genome shotgun. PLOS Comput. Biol. 1, e43 (2005)." href="/articles/ng.475#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d17306e3273">56</a></sup>, PILER-DF<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Edgar, R.C. &amp; Myers, E.W. PILER: identification and classification of genomic repeats. Bioinformatics 21 Suppl 1, i152âi158 (2005)." href="/articles/ng.475#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d17306e3277">57</a></sup>, RepeatScout<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Price, A.L., Jones, N.C. &amp; Pevzner, P.A. De novo identification of repeat families in large genomes. Bioinformatics 21 Suppl 1, i351âi358 (2005)." href="/articles/ng.475#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d17306e3281">58</a></sup> and LTR_Finder<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Xu, Z. &amp; Wang, H. LTR_FINDER: an efficient tool for the prediction of full-length LTR retrotransposons. Nucleic Acids Res. 35, W265âW268 (2007)." href="/articles/ng.475#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d17306e3285">59</a></sup>, were used to search for repeat sequences within the cucumber genome. All repeat sequences with lengths &gt;100 bp and gap 'N' &lt;5% constituted the raw transposable element library.</p><p>The repeat elements belonging to rRNA and satellite sequences were first filtered using BLASTN (<i>E</i> value â¤ 1 Ã 10<sup>â10</sup>, identity â¥ 80%, coverage â¥ 50% and minimal matching length â¥ 100 bp). All-versus-all BLASTN (<i>E</i> value â¤ 1 Ã 10<sup>â10</sup>) searches were then conducted iteratively, and the shorter sequences were filtered when two repeats aligned with identity â¥ 80%, coverage â¥ 80% and minimal matching length â¥ 100 bp; this yielded a nonredundant transposable element library. The nonredundant repeats were then searched against the Swiss-Prot protein database to filter the protein-coding genes by BLASTX (<i>E</i> value â¤ 1 Ã 10<sup>â4</sup>, identity â¥ 30%, coverage â¥ 30% and minimal matching length â¥ 30 amino acids). After manual curation, a <i>de novo</i> transposable element library for cucumber was obtained.</p><p>Transposable elements in the cucumber genome assembly were identified both at the DNA and protein level. RepeatMasker was applied for DNA-level identification using a custom library (a combination of Repbase, plant repeat database and our cucumber <i>de novo</i> transposable element library). At the protein level, RepeatProteinMask was used to conduct WU-BLASTX searches against the transposable element protein database. Overlapping transposable elements belonging to the same type of repeats were integrated together, whereas those with low scores were removed if they overlapped &gt;80% and belonged to different types.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec23">Gene prediction.</h3><p>Our strategy for gene prediction was to conduct <i>de novo</i> predictions on the repeat-masked genome and then integrate them with spliced alignments of proteins and transcripts to genome sequences using GLEAN<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Elsik, C.G. et al. Creating a honey bee consensus gene set. Genome Biol. 8, R13 (2007)." href="/articles/ng.475#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d17306e3328">60</a></sup>. Cucumber genome sequences were masked by identified repeat sequences with length &gt;500 bp, except for miniature inverted-repeat transposable elements, which are usually found near genes or inside introns. The EST and full-length cDNA sequences of cucumber were processed by PASA<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Campbell, M.A., Haas, B.J., Hamilton, J.P., Mount, S.M. &amp; Buell, C.R. Comprehensive analysis of alternative splicing in rice and comparative analyses with Arabidopsis. BMC Genomics 7, 327 (2006)." href="/articles/ng.475#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d17306e3332">61</a></sup> to train gene prediction software BGF<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Li, H. et al. Test data sets and evaluation of gene prediction programs on the rice genome. J Comp Sci Tech 20, 446â453 (2005)." href="/articles/ng.475#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d17306e3336">62</a></sup>, GlimmerHMM<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Majoros, W.H., Pertea, M. &amp; Salzberg, S.L. TigrScan and GlimmerHMM: two open source ab initio eukaryotic gene-finders. Bioinformatics 20, 2878â2879 (2004)." href="/articles/ng.475#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d17306e3340">63</a></sup> and SNAP<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="Korf, I. Gene finding in novel genomes. BMC Bioinformatics 5, 59 (2004)." href="/articles/ng.475#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d17306e3345">64</a></sup>. Augustus<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="Stanke, M. &amp; Waack, S. Gene prediction with a hidden Markov model and a new intron submodel. Bioinformatics 19 Suppl 2, ii215âii225 (2003)." href="/articles/ng.475#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d17306e3349">65</a></sup> and Genscan<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="Salamov, A.A. &amp; Solovyev, V.V. Ab initio gene finding in Drosophila genomic DNA. Genome Res. 10, 516â522 (2000)." href="/articles/ng.475#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d17306e3353">66</a></sup> software used gene model parameters trained for <i>Arabidopsis</i>. We aligned the protein sequences of five sequenced plants (<i>Arabidopsis</i>, papaya, poplar, grapevine and rice) onto the cucumber genome using TBLASTN, at an <i>E</i>-value cutoff of 1 Ã 10<sup>â5</sup>, and the homologous genome sequences were aligned against the matching proteins using GeneWise<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 67" title="Birney, E., Clamp, M. &amp; Durbin, R. GeneWise and Genomewise. Genome Res. 14, 988â995 (2004)." href="/articles/ng.475#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d17306e3369">67</a></sup> for accurate spliced alignments. The cDNA and EST sequences of cucumber and melon were aligned against the cucumber genome using BLAT (identity â¥ 0.95, coverage â¥ 0.90) to generate spliced alignments. We also aligned TIGR unigenes<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 68" title="Childs, K.L. et al. The TIGR Plant Transcript Assemblies database. Nucleic Acids Res. 35, D846âD851 (2007)." href="/articles/ng.475#ref-CR68" id="ref-link-section-d17306e3373">68</a></sup> from Cucurbitales, Fabales and Fagales to the cucumber genome by ATT_gap2 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="Huang, X., Adams, M.D., Zhou, H. &amp; Kerlavage, A.R. A tool for analyzing and annotating genomic sequences. Genomics 46, 37â45 (1997)." href="/articles/ng.475#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d17306e3376">69</a>). All of these resources were combined by GLEAN<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Elsik, C.G. et al. Creating a honey bee consensus gene set. Genome Biol. 8, R13 (2007)." href="/articles/ng.475#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d17306e3380">60</a></sup> to produce the consensus gene sets.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec24">Identification of noncoding RNA genes in the cucumber genome.</h3><p>The tRNA genes were identified by tRNAscan-SE<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 70" title="Lowe, T.M. &amp; Eddy, S.R. tRNAscan-SE: a program for improved detection of transfer RNA genes in genomic sequence. Nucleic Acids Res. 25, 955â964 (1997)." href="/articles/ng.475#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d17306e3392">70</a></sup> with default parameters. The C/D-box small nucleolar RNAs were identified by Snoscan<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 71" title="Lowe, T.M. &amp; Eddy, S.R. A computational screen for methylation guide snoRNAs in yeast. Science 283, 1168â1171 (1999)." href="/articles/ng.475#ref-CR71" id="ref-link-section-d17306e3396">71</a></sup> using yeast rRNA and yeast methylation sites. Other noncoding RNAs, including miRNA, small nuclear RNA and H/ACA-box small nucleolar RNA, were identified using INFERNAL software by searching against the Rfam<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 72" title="Griffiths-Jones, S. et al. Rfam: annotating non-coding RNAs in complete genomes. Nucleic Acids Res. 33, D121âD124 (2005)." href="/articles/ng.475#ref-CR72" id="ref-link-section-d17306e3400">72</a></sup> database with default parameters.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec25">Construction of gene families.</h3><p>We adapted the Treefam<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 73" title="Li, H. et al. TreeFam: a curated database of phylogenetic trees of animal gene families. Nucleic Acids Res. 34, D572âD580 (2006)." href="/articles/ng.475#ref-CR73" id="ref-link-section-d17306e3412">73</a></sup> method to construct gene families for the genes in cucumber, <i>Arabidopsis</i>, papaya, poplar, grapevine and rice (outgroup).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec26">Construction of syntenic blocks.</h3><p>We identified syntenic blocks between two species (A and B) by an automatic clustering algorithm on a dot plot graph, which included five steps. First, markers (gene pairs) were generated between A and B. All protein sequences of A were aligned to all proteins of B using BLASTP (<i>E</i> value &lt; 1 Ã 10<sup>â10</sup> and identity &gt; 20%). The fragmental alignments were conjoined for each gene pair. Those gene pairs with aligned regions covering &lt;50% were filtered. The remaining gene pairs were plotted on the dot graph as markers (points). Second, the Euclidean distance was calculated for each pair. Distances were calculated based on the gene order in each chromosome rather than the genomic position. Third, hierarchical clustering was determined for all of the points. If the distance between two points was less than the distance cutoff, a link was assigned. The distance cutoff was adapted in accordance with the selected species. Fourth, the quality was estimated for each cluster by calculating the point number (<i>N</i>), average point distance (<i>D</i>) and correlation coefficient (<i>R</i>). A score (<i>S</i>) was calculated to show the overall quality, defined as <i>S</i> = <i>N</i> Ã sqrt(2)/<i>D</i> Ã <i>R</i>. Finally, problematic clusters were filtered. Clusters with <i>N</i> &lt; 8 or |<i>R</i>| &lt; 0.5 were filtered out. The clusters caused by tandem duplication were further filtered by determining the slope (<i>L</i>) of the regression line within a range of 0.1 &lt; |<i>L</i>| &lt; 10. This algorithm can also be used to study intraspecies synteny.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec27">4DTv calculation.</h3><p>After the identification of syntenic blocks, the pairwise protein alignments for each gene pair were first constructed with MUSCLE<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 74" title="Edgar, R.C. MUSCLE: multiple sequence alignment with high accuracy and high throughput. Nucleic Acids Res. 32, 1792â1797 (2004)." href="/articles/ng.475#ref-CR74" id="ref-link-section-d17306e3479">74</a></sup>. The nucleotide alignment was then created according to the protein alignment. 4DTv was then calculated on concatenated nucleotide alignments with HKY substitution models<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 75" title="Hasegawa, M., Kishino, H. &amp; Yano, T. Dating of the human-ape splitting by a molecular clock of mitochondrial DNA. J. Mol. Evol. 22, 160â174 (1985)." href="/articles/ng.475#ref-CR75" id="ref-link-section-d17306e3483">75</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec28">Comparative analysis between cucumber and melon.</h3><p>Cucumber genome sequences were aligned with melon BAC sequences using NUCmer, a program in the MUMmer package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 76" title="Kurtz, S. et al. Versatile and open software for comparing large genomes. Genome Biol. 5, R12 (2004)." href="/articles/ng.475#ref-CR76" id="ref-link-section-d17306e3495">76</a></sup>. The delta-filter program was then run with the â1 option to remove complex alignments. Orthologous gene pairs were identified by the reciprocal best method.</p><p>The Bayesian relaxed molecular clock approach was used to estimate divergence time using the program MULTIDIVTIME, which was implemented using the Thornian Time Traveler (T3) package. The calibration time (fossil record time) interval (54â90 million years ago) of Capparales was obtained from previous results<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 77" title="Crepet, W.L., Nixon, K.C. &amp; Gandolfo, M.A. Fossil evidence and phylogeny: the age of major angiosperm clades based on mesofossil and macrofossil evidence from Cretaceous deposits. Am. J. Botany 91, 1666â1682 (2004)." href="/articles/ng.475#ref-CR77" id="ref-link-section-d17306e3502">77</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 78" title="WikstrÃ¶m, N., Savolainen, V. &amp; Chase, M.W. Evolution of the angiosperms: calibrating the family tree. Proc. Biol. Sci. 268, 2211â2220 (2001)." href="/articles/ng.475#ref-CR78" id="ref-link-section-d17306e3505">78</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec29">URLs.</h3><p><i>Arabidopsis thaliana</i> (TIGR Release 5.0), <a href="ftp://ftp.tigr.org/pub/data/a_thaliana/ath1">ftp://ftp.tigr.org/pub/data/a_thaliana/ath1</a>; <i>Carica papaya</i> (assembly v1.0, EVidence Modeler genes), <a href="http://www.life.uiuc.edu/ming">http://www.life.uiuc.edu/ming</a>; <i>Populus trichocarpa</i> (assembly release v1.0, annotation v1.1), <a href="http://genome.jgi-psf.org/Poptr1_1/Poptr1_1.download.ftp.html">http://genome.jgi-psf.org/Poptr1_1/Poptr1_1.download.ftp.html</a>; <i>Vitis vinifera</i> (published assembly, annotation v1), <a href="http://www.genoscope.cns.fr/externe/GenomeBrowser/Vitis/">http://www.genoscope.cns.fr/externe/GenomeBrowser/Vitis/</a>; <i>Oryza sativa</i> (assembly International Rice Genome Sequencing Project build 3), <a href="http://rgp.dna.affrc.go.jp/IRGSP/download.html">http://rgp.dna.affrc.go.jp/IRGSP/download.html</a>; UniGene sequences of <i>Cucurbitales</i>, <i>Fabales</i> and <i>Fagales</i>, <a href="http://plantta.jcvi.org/">http://plantta.jcvi.org/</a>; cucumber marker sequences, <a href="http://cucumber.genomics.org.cn">http://cucumber.genomics.org.cn</a>; KEGG release 47, <a href="ftp://ftp.genome.jp/pub/kegg/pathway/">ftp://ftp.genome.jp/pub/kegg/pathway/</a>; Repbase release 13.07, <a href="http://www.girinst.org/repbase/index.html">http://www.girinst.org/repbase/index.html</a>; Thornian Time Traveler (T3) package, <a href="http://abacus.gene.ucl.ac.uk/software.html">http://abacus.gene.ucl.ac.uk/software.html</a>; RepeatMasker, <a href="http://www.repeatmasker.org">http://www.repeatmasker.org</a>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec30">Accession codes.</h3><p>The cucumber genome sequence has been deposited in GenBank with accession code <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nuccore/?term=ACHR00000000">ACHR00000000</a> (the version described here is the first version, with accession code <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nuccore/?term=ACHR01000000">ACHR01000000</a>).</p><p><i>Note: </i><a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ng.475#MOESM303">
                    <i>Supplementary information</i>
                  </a><i> is available on the Nature Genetics website</i>.</p></div></div></section>

              <p class="c-article-further-reading__journal-title" id="journal-name-3">
                <i>Plants</i>
                (2021)
              </p>
            </li>
          
            <li class="c-article-further-reading__item js-ref-item" id="further-reading-item-4">
